\hypertarget{classRGESolver}{}\doxysection{R\+G\+E\+Solver Class Reference}
\label{classRGESolver}\index{RGESolver@{RGESolver}}

\begin{Indent}\textbf{ S\+M\+E\+FT dimension-\/six operators}\par
{\em By default, all S\+M\+E\+FT dimension-\/six operators\textquotesingle{} coefficients are set to 0. See \href{https://arxiv.org/abs/1308.2627}{\texttt{ https\+://arxiv.\+org/abs/1308.\+2627}} tab. 1 for the full list of operators. Each member has a class from 1 to 8 depending on its field contents, as well as a flavour symmetry classification (W\+C1, W\+C2R, W\+C2I...). ~\newline

\begin{Indent}\textbf{ Independent entries}\par
{\em We follow \href{https://arxiv.org/abs/2010.16341}{\texttt{ https\+://arxiv.\+org/abs/2010.\+16341}} tab. 15, 16 for the symmetry class of the operators. ~\newline
 Notice that operators in classes W\+C1 and W\+C5 have no restrictions for neither real nor imaginary part, each having $N_G ^2$ (for W\+C1) or $N_G ^4$ (for W\+C5). ~\newline

\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
A class that performs renormalization group evolution in the context of the S\+M\+E\+FT. 

The class solves the Renormalization Group Equations (R\+G\+Es) both numerically and in the leading-\/log approximations. Only operators up to dimension six that preserve lepton and baryon numbers are considered. The operator basis is the Warsaw basis, defined in \href{https://arxiv.org/abs/1008.4884}{\texttt{ https\+://arxiv.\+org/abs/1008.\+4884}}. ~\newline
 The user must set separately real and imaginary part of each complex parameter. ~\newline
 In tables \ref{SM}, \ref{0F}, \ref{2F} and \ref{4F} are listed all the parameters, together with their name (that must be used to correctly invoke getter and setter functions). ~\newline
The numerical integration is performed with an adaptive step-\/size routine (the Explicit embedded Runge-\/\+Kutta-\/\+Fehlberg method), using the tools in the G\+NU Scientific Library. ~\newline
 See \href{https://www.gnu.org/software/gsl/doc/html/ode-initval.html}{\texttt{ https\+://www.\+gnu.\+org/software/gsl/doc/html/ode-\/initval.\+html}} for all the details. ~\newline
The accuracy level of the numerical integration can be tuned selecting the parameters $\epsilon_{rel}, \epsilon_{abs}$ and the integration step using the dedicated getter functions.

H\+E\+Pfit Collaboration 
\end{DoxyAuthor}

G\+NU General Public License

Coefficient     & \multicolumn{1}{c}{Name}      \\ \hline 
$g_1$         & \texttt{g1}      \\

\mbox{\Hypertarget{classRGESolver_aedc6f80d9a01de09d4ddf1e5b670c690}\label{classRGESolver_aedc6f80d9a01de09d4ddf1e5b670c690}} 
\index{RGESolver@{RGESolver}!Evolve@{Evolve}}
\index{Evolve@{Evolve}!RGESolver@{RGESolver}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Evolve()}{Evolve()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void R\+G\+E\+Solver\+::\+Evolve (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::string}]{method,  }\item[{double}]{muI,  }\item[{double}]{muF }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Command to perform the R\+GE evolution. 

R\+G\+Es are solved with the chosen method from {\ttfamily muI} to {\ttfamily muF}. Currently, the available methods are \char`\"{}\+Numeric\char`\"{} and \char`\"{}\+Leading-\/\+Log\char`\"{}. ~\newline
 The evolutor takes as initial values the current values of the parameters, set with the {\ttfamily Set\+Coefficient(...)} function. After completing the evolution the values of the parameters are updated and are accessible with the {\ttfamily Get\+Coefficient(...)} function. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em method} & resolution method \\
\hline
{\em muI} & initial energy scale \\
\hline
{\em muF} & final energy scale \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{classRGESolver_a7c0c4303beb14f728a70542c8583b3a7}\label{classRGESolver_a7c0c4303beb14f728a70542c8583b3a7}} 
\index{RGESolver@{RGESolver}!EvolveSMOnly@{EvolveSMOnly}}
\index{EvolveSMOnly@{EvolveSMOnly}!RGESolver@{RGESolver}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EvolveSMOnly()}{EvolveSMOnly()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void R\+G\+E\+Solver\+::\+Evolve\+S\+M\+Only (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::string}]{method,  }\item[{double}]{muI,  }\item[{double}]{muF }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Same as \mbox{\hyperlink{classRGESolver_aedc6f80d9a01de09d4ddf1e5b670c690}{Evolve(std\+::string method, double mu\+I, double mu\+F)}}, but only for the SM parameters. The user should use this method instead of {\ttfamily Evolve} when interested in pure SM running. ~\newline
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em method} & \\
\hline
{\em muI} & \\
\hline
{\em muF} & \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily void R\+G\+E\+Solver\+::\+Generate\+S\+M\+Initial\+Conditions (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{mu,  }\item[{std\+::string}]{basis,  }\item[{std\+::string}]{method,  }\item[{bool}]{input\+C\+KM = {\ttfamily true} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates the initial conditions for Standard Model\textquotesingle{}s parameters (gauge couplings, Yukawa coupling, quartic coupling and Higgs\textquotesingle{} boson mass). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em mu} & Scale (in GeV) at which the initial conditions are generated. If {\ttfamily mu} is different from the scale at which the input is given, {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classRGESolver}{R\+G\+E\+Solver}}} will use the pure SM R\+G\+Es to run the parameters to the scale {\ttfamily mu}. \\
\hline
{\em basis} & Flavour basis ( {\ttfamily \char`\"{}\+U\+P\char`\"{}{\ttfamily  or {\ttfamily \char`\"{}\+D\+O\+W\+N\char`\"{}}) }}\\
\hline
{\em method} & {\ttfamily {\ttfamily Method used by {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classRGESolver}{R\+G\+E\+Solver}}} to run the SM parameters to the scale {\ttfamily mu} ({\ttfamily \char`\"{}\+Numeric\char`\"{}} or {\ttfamily \char`\"{}\+Leading-\/\+Log\char`\"{}}) }}\\
\hline
{\em input\+C\+KM} & {\ttfamily {\ttfamily If set to {\ttfamily true} (default), the input for the Yukawa matrices will be generated from the current value of the C\+KM matrix and the masses of the fermions (default). ~\newline
 }}\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{GetCoefficient()}{GetCoefficient()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily double R\+G\+E\+Solver\+::\+Get\+Coefficient (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::string}]{name }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Getter function for scalar/0F parameters (no flavour indices). 

If the parameter name does not match with any of the parameters, an error message is printed and the value 0 is returned. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em name} & name of the parameter \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the requested parameter (if it exists), otherwise returns 0. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
